#### # Instructions  
####   
#### A circular buffer, cyclic buffer or ring buffer is a data structure that uses a single, fixed-size buffer as if it were connected end-to-end.  
####   
#### A circular buffer first starts empty and of some predefined length.  
#### For example, this is a 7-element buffer:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Assume that a 1 is written into the middle of the buffer (exact starting location does not matter in a circular buffer):  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][1][ ][ ][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Then assume that two more elements are added — 2 & 3 — which get appended after the 1:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][1][2][3][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### If two elements are then removed from the buffer, the oldest values inside the buffer are removed.  
#### The two elements removed, in this case, are 1 & 2, leaving the buffer with just a 3:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][ ][ ][ ][3][ ]  
#### ```  
####   
#### If the buffer has 7 elements then it is completely full:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [5][6][7][8][9][3][4]  
#### ```  
####   
#### When the buffer is full an error will be raised, alerting the client that further writes are blocked until a slot becomes free.  
####   
#### When the buffer is full, the client can opt to overwrite the oldest data with a forced write.  
#### In this case, two more elements — A & B — are added and they overwrite the 3 & 4:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [5][6][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### 3 & 4 have been replaced by A & B making 5 now the oldest data in the buffer.  
#### Finally, if two elements are removed then what would be returned is 5 & 6 yielding the buffer:  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [ ][ ][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### Because there is space available, if the client again uses overwrite to store C & D then the space where 5 & 6 were stored previously will be used not the location of 7 & 8.  
#### 7 is still the oldest element and the buffer is once again full.  
####   
#### ```text  
#### [C][D][7][8][9][A][B]  
#### ```  
####   
#### ####  
####   
#### Use the above instructions to modify the supplied files: circular_buffer.cpp circular_buffer.h  
#### Don't change the names of existing functions or classes, as they may be referenced from other code like unit tests, etc.  
#### Only use standard libraries, don't suggest installing any packages.

```cpp
class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity);
    T read();

    void overwrite(const T& data);
    void clear();

    bool full() const;

    size_t read_pos;
    size_t write_pos;

    size_t capacity_;
};
```

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity);
    T read();
    void write(const T& data);
    void overwrite(const T& data);
    void clear();
    bool empty() const;
    bool full() const;
    
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    size_t read_pos;
    size_t write_pos;
    size_t num_elements;
    size_t capacity_;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity) 
        : buffer(capacity), read_pos(0), write_pos(0), num_elements(0), capacity_(capacity) {
    }
    
    T read() {
        if (empty()) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
        }
        T value = buffer[read_pos];
        read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity_;
        --num_elements;
        return value;
    }
    
    void write(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
        }
        buffer[write_pos] = data;
        write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity_;
        ++num_elements;
    }
    
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            // If full, we need to advance the read position
            buffer[write_pos] = data;
            write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity_;
            read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity_;
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }
    
    void clear() {
        read_pos = 0;
        write_pos = 0;
        num_elements = 0;
    }
    
    bool empty() const {
        return num_elements == 0;
    }
    
    bool full() const {
        return num_elements == capacity_;
    }
    
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    size_t read_pos;
    size_t write_pos;
    size_t num_elements;
    size_t capacity_;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity) 
        : buffer(capacity), read_pos(0), write_pos(0), num_elements(0), capacity_(capacity) {
    }
    
    T read() {
        if (empty()) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
        }
        T value = buffer[read_pos];
        read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity_;
        --num_elements;
        return value;
    }
    
    void write(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
        }
        buffer[write_pos] = data;
        write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity_;
        ++num_elements;
    }
    
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            // If full, we need to advance the read position
            buffer[write_pos] = data;
            write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity_;
            read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity_;
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }
    
    void clear() {
        read_pos = 0;
        write_pos = 0;
        num_elements = 0;
    }
    
    bool empty() const {
        return num_elements == 0;
    }
    
    bool full() const {
        return num_elements == capacity_;
    }
    
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer;
    size_t read_pos;
    size_t write_pos;
    size_t num_elements;
    size_t capacity_;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity);
    int read();
    void write(int data);
    void overwrite(int data);
    void clear();
    bool empty() const;
    bool full() const;
    
private:
    std::vector<int> buffer;
    size_t read_pos;
    size_t write_pos;
    size_t num_elements;
    size_t capacity_;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
```

Now, let's implement these methods in the .cpp file:

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"

namespace circular_buffer {

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(size_t capacity) 
    : buffer(capacity), read_pos(0), write_pos(0), num_elements(0), capacity_(capacity) {
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (empty()) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[read_pos];
    read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity_;
    --num_elements;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int data) {
    if (full()) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[write_pos] = data;
    write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity_;
    ++num_elements;
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full()) {
        // Overwrite the oldest element and advance read position
        buffer[write_pos] = data;
        write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity_;
        read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity_;
    } else {
        write(data);
    }
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    read_pos = 0;
    write_pos = 0;
    num_elements = 0;
}

bool circular_buffer::empty() const {
    return num_elements == 0;
}

bool circular_buffer::full() const {
    return num_elements == capacity_;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

4. Maintained error handling for empty reads and full writes

But in our implementation, when the buffer is full, we're writing to the current write position and then advancing both read and write pointers.
This seems correct.

However, the number of elements (`num_elements`) remains the same when overwriting while full, which is correct because we're replacing one element.
But in our implementation, when full, we're not changing `num_elements` which is correct since the number of elements doesn't change when overwriting.

Wait, but when the buffer is not full, we call `write()` which increments `num_elements`.

Let's test our implementation against the provided example:
1. Start with empty buffer of size 7
2. Write 1 to the middle: This depends on where write_pos starts (0)
   Our implementation always starts at index 0, so to write to the middle, we need to adjust
   But the instructions say the exact starting location doesn't matter
3. Write 2 and 3: These will be at indices 1 and 2
4. Remove two elements: read from index 0 and 1 (values 1 and 2)
   read_pos becomes 2, num_elements becomes 1
5. Write until full: Write 5,6,7,8,9 at indices 3,4,5,6,0
   But wait, our implementation uses modulo arithmetic, so after index 6 comes index 0
   num_elements becomes 6
   But the buffer capacity is 7, so we can write one more
   The example says it's full with 7 elements, which matches
6. Overwrite with A and B: These should overwrite the oldest elements which are at read_pos (2)
   But in our implementation, we write to write_pos which is at index 1 (after writing 9 at index 0)
   So we write A at index 1, then B at index 2, advancing read_pos to 4
   This doesn't match the example where 3 and 4 should be overwritten

This suggests our implementation may not be correct for the overwrite operation.
When the buffer is full, overwrite should behave like writing, but it needs to also advance the read pointer to "evict" the oldest element.

Wait, the correct implementation should, when full during overwrite:
1. Write to the current write position
2. Advance write pointer
3. If the buffer was full, advance read pointer (because we're overwriting the oldest element)
   But this doesn't seem to track which is the oldest element correctly

Actually, a better approach is to always write, and if the buffer is full, then also advance the read pointer
But this matches our implementation

Wait, the issue is that when we overwrite, we always write to write_pos, which may not be where the oldest element is
In a circular buffer, the oldest element is at read_pos when full
So to overwrite the oldest element, we should be writing to read_pos and advancing both pointers
But that's not what we're doing

This suggests our implementation is incorrect
Let's fix the overwrite implementation:

When overwriting:
1. If the buffer is full, we need to write at the read_pos and advance both read and write pointers
2. But this doesn't match the example where new writes should go to the next available position after the last write

Wait, the example says that when using overwrite to store C & D, they should go where 5 & 6 were stored, not where 7 & 8 are
This suggests that write_pos should always point to the next available slot, and when overwriting, we advance read_pos

So the correct implementation for overwrite is:
1. If the buffer is full, read() first to make space, then write()
2. Or simply always write, and if full, advance read_pos

Here's the fix:

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full()) {
        // Overwrite the oldest element and advance read position
        buffer[write_pos] = data;
        write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity_;
        read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity_;
    } else {
        write(data);
    }
}
=======
void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full()) {
        // Read the oldest element to effectively remove it, then write normally
        // But we don't want to actually return the value, just make space
        read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity_;
        num_elements--;
    }
    // Now we can write which will handle the rest
    write(data);
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

But this implementation may not be the most efficient, but it ensures that when the buffer is full, we make space for one new element by advancing the read pointer, which removes the oldest element.
Then we can write the new data which will behave as normal.

This should now match the example:
When the buffer is full and we overwrite, the oldest element is effectively removed, making space for the new write
Thus, the write will go to the current write_pos, which is correct

Let's test this with the example where the buffer is full:
[5][6][7][8][9][3][4] (indices may vary)
read_pos points to the oldest element (5)
Overwrite A:
   Advance read_pos to point to 6, decrement num_elements to 6
   Write A to write_pos (which is where? After 4 it would be index 0 if we've been writing sequentially)
   But in our implementation, write_pos always points to the next available slot
   So we write A, increment write_pos and num_elements
   Now the buffer contains [A][6][7][8][9][3][4] with read_pos at index 1, write_pos at index 1, num_elements=7
Overwrite B:
   Advance read_pos to index 2, decrement num_elements to 6
   Write B to write_pos (index 1)
   Now the buffer contains [A][B][7][8][9][3][4] with read_pos at index 2, write_pos at index 2, num_elements=7

This matches the example where A and B overwrite 5 and 6, making 7 the oldest element

This seems correct. Let's proceed with this implementation.

I understand the issue. The tests are expecting a templated implementation, but our implementation uses `int` specifically. Let's fix that by making the implementation templated and moving the implementation into the header file.

Here are the necessary changes:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity);
    int read();
    void write(int data);
    void overwrite(int data);
    void clear();
    bool empty() const;
    bool full() const;
    
private:
    std::vector<int> buffer;
    size_t read_pos;
    size_t write_pos;
    size_t num_elements;
    size_t capacity_;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
=======
#if !defined(CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H)
#define CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H

#include <vector>
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

template <typename T>
class circular_buffer {
public:
    explicit circular_buffer(size_t capacity) 
        : buffer_(capacity), read_pos_(0), write_pos_(0), size_(0), capacity_(capacity) {
    }
    
    T read() {
        if (empty()) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
        }
        T value = buffer_[read_pos_];
        read_pos_ = (read_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
        --size_;
        return value;
    }
    
    void write(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
        }
        buffer_[write_pos_] = data;
        write_pos_ = (write_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
        ++size_;
    }
    
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            // Read the oldest element to effectively remove it, then write normally
            read_pos_ = (read_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            --size_;
        }
        // Now we can write which will handle the rest
        write(data);
    }
    
    void clear() {
        read_pos_ = 0;
        write_pos_ = 0;
        size_ = 0;
    }
    
    bool empty() const {
        return size_ == 0;
    }
    
    bool full() const {
        return size_ == capacity_;
    }
    
private:
    std::vector<T> buffer_;
    size_t read_pos_;
    size_t write_pos_;
    size_t size_;
    size_t capacity_;
};

}  // namespace circular_buffer

#endif // CIRCULAR_BUFFER_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

circular_buffer.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "circular_buffer.h"
#include <stdexcept>

namespace circular_buffer {

circular_buffer::circular_buffer(size_t capacity) 
    : buffer(capacity), read_pos(0), write_pos(0), num_elements(0), capacity_(capacity) {
}

int circular_buffer::read() {
    if (empty()) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is empty");
    }
    int value = buffer[read_pos];
    read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity_;
    --num_elements;
    return value;
}

void circular_buffer::write(int data) {
    if (full()) {
        throw std::domain_error("Buffer is full");
    }
    buffer[write_pos] = data;
    write_pos = (write_pos + 1) % capacity_;
    ++num_elements;
}

void circular_buffer::overwrite(int data) {
    if (full()) {
        // Read the oldest element to effectively remove it, then write normally
        // But we don't want to actually return the value, just make space
        read_pos = (read_pos + 1) % capacity_;
        num_elements--;
    }
    // Now we can write which will handle the rest
    write(data);
}

void circular_buffer::clear() {
    read_pos = 0;
    write_pos = 0;
    num_elements = 0;
}

bool circular_buffer::empty() const {
    return num_elements == 0;
}

bool circular_buffer::full() const {
    return num_elements == capacity_;
}

}  // namespace circular_buffer
=======
#include "circular_buffer.h"

namespace circular_buffer {

// Implementation is now in the header file due to templating

}  // namespace circular_buffer
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation:
1. Makes the `circular_buffer` class templated to work with any type, not just `int`
2. Moves all implementation into the header file (necessary for templates)
3. Keeps the same logic for buffer operations
4. Uses `const T&` for write and overwrite parameters to avoid unnecessary copying
5. Updates variable names to be more consistent (using trailing underscores for member variables)

This should now work with the tests that expect to use different types like `int` and `std::string`. The implementation handles the core functionality of a circular buffer while being flexible enough to work with any data type.

```cpp
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            // When full, the oldest element is at read_pos_, so we overwrite it
            buffer_[write_pos_] = data;
            write_pos_ = (write_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            read_pos_ = write_pos_; // The oldest element is now at the next position
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }
```

Actually, the correct implementation should be:
1. If the buffer is full, the next write will overwrite the oldest element which is at `read_pos_`
2. So we need to write to the current `write_pos_` (which is where the next element should go)
3. Then advance both `read_pos_` and `write_pos_` to maintain the circular nature
4. But `read_pos_` should now point to the next oldest element

circular_buffer.h

```cpp
            read_pos_ = write_pos_;
        } else {

        if (full()) {
            // Write the data, which will overwrite the element at write_pos_
            buffer_[write_pos_] = data;
            // Advance both pointers since we're overwriting the oldest element
            write_pos_ = (write_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
```

I understand. The issue is with the `overwrite` implementation. When the buffer is full, we need to overwrite the oldest element, which is at `read_pos_`, not at `write_pos_`. Let's fix that.

Here's the correct implementation:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            // Write the data, which will overwrite the element at write_pos_
            buffer_[write_pos_] = data;
            // Advance both pointers since we're overwriting the oldest element
            write_pos_ = (write_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            read_pos_ = write_pos_;
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }
=======
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            // Overwrite the oldest element at read_pos_ and advance read_pos_
            buffer_[read_pos_] = data;
            read_pos_ = (read_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            write_pos_ = read_pos_;
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

However, this may not be correct either. When the buffer is full, the oldest element is at `read_pos_`, so we should overwrite that.
But then we need to advance both pointers to maintain consistency.

Wait, the correct approach is:
1. If the buffer is full, the next write should overwrite the oldest element which is at `read_pos_`
2. Write the new data to the current `write_pos_` (which may not be the same as `read_pos_`)
3. Advance both pointers to maintain the circular nature

Actually, when the buffer is full, `read_pos_` and `write_pos_` point to the same element
So we can write to `write_pos_`, then advance both pointers

Here's a better implementation:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            // Overwrite the oldest element at read_pos_ and advance read_pos_
            buffer_[read_pos_] = data;
            read_pos_ = (read_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            write_pos_ = read_pos_;
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }
=======
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            // Write the data to the current write position, which will overwrite the oldest element
            buffer_[write_pos_] = data;
            // Advance both pointers to maintain the circular nature
            write_pos_ = (write_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            read_pos_ = write_pos_;
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Wait, this is the same as before. Let's think differently.
When the buffer is full, `read_pos_` points to the oldest element, and `write_pos_` points to where the next write would go
But since the buffer is full, `write_pos_` and `read_pos_` are the same
So we can write to `write_pos_`, then advance both pointers

But to always have `read_pos_` point to the oldest element, we need to advance it as well
So:

circular_buffer.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            // Write the data to the current write position, which will overwrite the oldest element
            buffer_[write_pos_] = data;
            // Advance both pointers to maintain the circular nature
            write_pos_ = (write_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            read_pos_ = write_pos_;
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }
=======
    void overwrite(const T& data) {
        if (full()) {
            // Write the data to the current write position
            buffer_[write_pos_] = data;
            // Advance write pointer
            write_pos_ = (write_pos_ + 1) % capacity_;
            // The oldest element is now the next one after the current read position
            read_pos_ = write_pos_;
        } else {
            write(data);
        }
    }
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation should work. Let's test it with the example:
Buffer is full: [5][6][7][8][9][3][4] (read_pos_=0, write_pos_=0)
Overwrite 'A': write to index 0 -> 'A', advance write_pos_ to 1, set read_pos_ to 1
Buffer: [A][6][7][8][9][3][4] (read_pos_=1, write_pos_=1)
Overwrite 'B': write to index 1 -> 'B', advance write_pos_ to 2, set read_pos_ to 2
Buffer: [A][B][7][8][9][3][4] (read_pos_=2, write_pos_=2)

This matches the example where 'A' and 'B' overwrote '5' and '6', making '7' the oldest element at index 2
Since read_pos_ is at 2, the next read will be from index 2 which is '7'

This seems correct. Let's proceed with this implementation.
